< Rating>
5</Rating>
<Pictures>None<//Pictures>< review>
If you know how to order Szechuan food rather than Americanized Chinese that's sweet, fried and boring then come here and don't order off just the big menu. But a few things are too good to pass on. Order Pot Stickers, made fresh, in house and taste like it (not like a trip to Costco's freezer was made) but an improvement would be Red Wine Vinegar. Egg Rolls made correctly. Fried Wontons, best I've found and kids will love them. Hot & Sour, Chicken & Corn, Wor Won Ton & Seafood soups  warm you on any winter night (just a touch of white "NOT BLACK" pepper in broth soups changes everything for the good). If you still eat meat then Tangerine Chicken, Cumin Beef & Yu-Shiang Pork are a must.

Now the good stuff like Kung Pao Fish, Salt & Pepper Fish w/Green Beans, Hot Braised Tofu & Garlic Eggplant w/Tofu. Fried Rice? WHY? Just get something worthwhile like Seafood Chow Fun or Hong Kong Style Pan Fried Noodles. You want plain rice for dishes w/sauce anyway, or your just killing the flavor of dishes you ordered because you like the sauce.

1, 2 or 3 ratings will go up to 4 or higher if you low raters will come back and try the Szechuan menu. Ask for the little menu, and liking heat is a requirement. Ask questions before ordering something, heat can be turned down if you just ask. Like salt, you can add but can't remove. It's just like when you first went for Thai and learned the heat levels that you liked. But in Szechuan the chefs make it as it has been made for centuries. So it's your job to say hold some on the heat, not there's to inquire what you want. Work together and all will be happy and great food will come to your table.

As to what to order, Try doing this, order a meal that you know will be enjoyed. Then order one dish that's new for you from the Szechuan menu or the other each trip. That way you aren't wasting any big amount, just spending a little and hopefully expanding your palate on something new. But there are things that you just have to try. Dan Dan Noodles are great and HOT! Kimchi is a dream.

I don't eat much in meat anymore, except I'm curious and tried the intestines. I was surprised and liked the dish. I would have them again, but I dine alone and I want more than a dish for dinner, so next time I'll want others with me who are willing. There are a few things I've tried and liked in meat, most are on both menus and I've stated them already. That said, try the Chicken or Fish Hot Pots (SO GOOD).

This next item has been taken off the new menu I saw, and asked why. It's because nobody orders it. Please ask if they will make you the Double Cooked Fish and maybe we can get it back on. I can only order if others are with me. It feeds three easy and I'm generally alone, leftover fish from any place "NO THANKS". So I'm careful in what I order. But this dish is worth eating leftovers for once in awhile. It's really that good if you like fish. I love fish so this menu is great because there is more fish than shrimp on it. The big menu has all the shrimp dishes. ENJOY!

So please don't bad mouth the place till you learn what is being brought to Sacramento that's not available much, if at all. Local mom & pops need us, new owners are just that, NEW. We are there teachers as much as they teach us what's new. If we all learn to talk and hear, our little world gets better. The Corp. chains don't care about us, just our wallets. Perhaps what is needed is for another chef who cooks Cantonese and/or Mandarin shows the Szechuan chefs what's wrong in the cooking of these foods.

Make sure someone with power knows you expected different, why this is unexceptable. Ask why the difference. Tell them this time to please remove it off your bill (Don't eat half first). Then say you'll try them and the dish again and hope things improved. If same then they lose your business and you will write poor reviews on several sites. This is your power.

It's our neighborhood. If we support mom & pops, then we should be heard and told without attitude "BOTH WAYS" why something can or cannot change.

Will the corporations do that?< /review>

The food was great the owners were nice it was like a mom and pop restaurant. However, recently we had food that was delivered that was not to our liking. < review>
Equipment is good, and they have a variety of stations to use. The only annoyance is the staff, who obviously don't use any type of lifting equipment in their life, come around interrupting your set of lifting to tell you how to use it properly and to move it. I'm sorry, are you telling me how to lift and what causes a hazard? When you actually have a healthy lifestyle of eating right and weightlifting experience, then you can interrupt my session to tell me I'm doing it wrong. Ive been lifting for 12years, dnt need them telling me how to and how not to lift. There's no reasoning with them. The little hawaiian/hispanic lady, not to be rude, started a fit about the placement of my equipment. It was NOT a hazard, but she was on my case about moving it, and gave the impression she was going to kick me out. I asked the guy staff that was there about the rules of equipment placement, they dnt have any. He showed me other placements, but those were more hazardous then where I had mine. I stated "theres no reasoning with yall, is there, just have to do it where you want huh?" And he said yes...<//review>

< Text>
Probably the worst gym I have been to in the Air Force. Granted I've only been to 8 AF gyms, but of the 8 this is the worst. Not enough machines/weights and the ones they do have are extremely close together making everything very crowded. The flow is very disorganized. I know I shouldn't complain, because it is free, but sometime free is not better. I know many people who pay out of pocket to go downtown so they avoid the on base gym.</Text>

<UserId.>103864140805162040494</UserId.>< user_name>
Mireille duclos< /user_name>
< Date>
1477515164732</Date>
<rating>5<//rating>< Text>
I have been using Blue Apron for about 14 months now.  I LOVE it!  I come home from work too tired and stressed to cook a "from scratch" dinner, let alone try to get creative.  We were in a rut of eating too many fast foods and the same "go to" recipes all the time.  With Blue Apron, I know that in 30 minutes I will be serving a gourmet quality meal.  It has pushed me outside my comfort zone in terms of ingredients and methods.  I call it my "leap of faith" because I often thing "eew" when I see the food listed but I can guarantee that every time it's going to be amazing!  I also appreciate the freshness of the ingredients and the fact that a high percentage of the ingredients are organic, grass fed and locally produced.   And though I've been cooking for decades, I've learning all kinds of new techniques - like how to cook an entire meal with one pot and one frying pan by wiping it out in between ingredients.  And I've used more shallots and lemons in the last year than I did in 30 years before that!!!  The customer service is great.  The few times I've had an issue with missing ingredients, I've had a response within hours and the problems have always been resolved to my satisfaction.<//Text>

<name>Kontji Anthony<//name><time>1471663620553< /time>< Review>
I highly recommend Blue Apron.  The meals are DELICIOUS!  Keep in mind that you do all of the food preparation from scratch.

I would call this a food shopping service.  The good thing is all the meals are 500 to 700 calories and they're wonderfully seasoned.

You choose if you like meat, poultry, fish and other preferences and Blue Apron plans your menus and mails you a box of food, spices and directions.  I did have to have my own salt, pepper and olive oil for my meals.

I did the 2-Person Plan, which offers two meals for three days at six meals total.  It cost $59.94 and shipping is always free.

You can also choose the Family Plan, which serves four.  Eight meals total cost $69.92 per delivery.

Blue Apron also offers wine pairing with your meals.  I didn't try that, so I can't tell you how that goes.

I have to say the ingredients are always very fresh.  The meals are packaged in a container that keeps the heat out and your food is sandwiched between two slabs of ice.

I had to cancel my meals because I was going to be unable to find time to cook, but I still got one delivery because I was a little too late.  You can reactivate with ease.

I did find that chopping, shredding and other preparation took longer than the directions indicated.

Still, if you have the time to make your own meals from start to finish, Blue Apron is definitely worth it!<//Review>

< rate>

<review>Was offered 2 free meals in the mail and by email.
Tried to get the free meals but was told I need to order 6 meals in order to get the 2 free ones.
This is not quite kosher to me especially the "other conditions" are buried in the fine prints..
IMO, this contradicts to what FTC refers to "free" -
Free Products
A product that's advertised as free if another is purchased - "buy one, get one" - indicates that the consumer will pay nothing for the one item and no more than the regular price for the other. Ads like these should describe all the terms and conditions of the free offer clearly and prominently.

<UserId.>104641601146023314946<//UserId.><username>Just Depends Content Creating</username><Time>1619409195477<//Time><rate>5<//rate><Text>So the funny thing is I found out about this place during my Single Ladies Days when a MAGICIAN from Tinder took me to the Sunset Blvd location for our first and only date lol.

It was my first time trying this location, and let me tell you, I was not disappointed! The location is more humble, but the quality is superior to any other sushi we have had in California (Sugarfish just doesn't disappoint you!)

The "Don't Think, Just Eat" is the best way to go, but IF you can stomach it (and I believe in you!) GET THE SEASONAL AND DAILY SPECIALS toooo! :) and definitely pairing with a hot green tea, they had YAMA MOTO YAMA green tea (one of my faves) when I went in today.

This is a sushi restaurant that pays attention to the quality of the cuts and ingredients and with intent. I didn't find myself dipping in extra sauces, rather just enjoying the sushi for what it is, which is their goal. Sugarfish has a propensity to go above and beyond, serving you emotions on a plate, and man, oh, man, I couldn't control my smile and dancing lol!

And oh my goodness, their daily special of the big scallop sushi today was devine!!! However, I was happily surprised by the garnish under the salmon skin sushi! The eel, truth be told, wasn't my fave, but I just don't like eel so you might love it! My boyfriend inhaled it lmao.

Carlos was our wonderful server, as is all the staff, he was exceptionally sweet, attentive, funny, and had wonderful timing.

Literally my only complaint is that while the 16% tip is already included, you can't add more, and BOY do I wish we could tip MORE without breaking their "no tipping rule." They're just so wonderful! Let me throw money at your servers Sugarfish lol.<//Text>< Pictures>

< Text>
Absolutely the best customer service and fresh fish I've had from all their locations.

DISCLAIMER I was a new walk up customer, not a food app pick up or pre-order and didn't know that other locations don't take walk up orders.

The manager took my order with a smile  (I can see it thru the mask) and was incredibly friendly. I mean beyond friendly. I even asked where I could use a restroom near by assuming they don't allow customers to use the restroom and he immediately said "come on in". He made me feel like a regular as if my order was the most important order of the day.

LA...this experience doesn't happen to often and I'm sure you'll a agree especially because I'm a new customer to the location passing through from a work meeting in the valley heading back to DTLA.

100 stars for the management team! I'd drive back just for you guys! Which I probably will do this weekend.

I went back to sugar fish in DTLA in the evening with my daughter for dinner because I was so happy with my experience ...you'll have to read what happened on their yelp.

Cheers to Sugarfish Studio City. Keep the food vibes com'n!!!<//Text>

< Review>
First time at SUGARFISH... It exceeded expectations. It's been on my list for quite a while, but haven't gone because I just never wanted to sit and wait forever on a busy Friday/Saturday night.

Took my chances and it was my lucky day! Came and got sat immediately! Thank God, because the hangry girl was about to come out.

"Don't Think. Just Eat"
- Handrolls
- Sashimi
- Nigiri

Can we get one in Orange County pleassseeee??!!!< /Review>

< Review>
Sugar fish used to be amazing. After Nozawa retired from his restaurant and his sons' chain (Sugar Fish) took over, they kept the amazing quality of fish that people had come to expect from Sushi Nozawa; however, as Sugar Fish has continued to grow, their quality has diminished. They are still a delicious option for sushi in LA, but Kiwami (down the street) has better quality fish. The one thing that Sugar fish does have going for it is their amazing to-go boxes which are beautifully packaged and taste great even after a car ride.<//Review>

<date>1535993380097< /date><Rate>4</Rate><Review>Easy to order menu. The trustme (omakase style) is just about the right portion size to leave you full but not overly stuffed. The fish selection may change so dont get too attached to what you see on the online menus. The fish is pretty good, so you may want to add a few pieces once your courses are completed. The Nozawa super dry sake comes in an 6 oz bottle. Fills ~3 1/2 sake cups, so plan accordingly so your 4th doesn't feel left out.

Not a huge space so the wait time for a table can be a bit long. Valet parking in the small plaza is $5, but you can find parking on a side street pretty readily.<//Review>< Pictures>

< Review>
I think everyone knows their "Trust Me" dish. I came twice, one time for dinner and lunch. Dinner was maybe 5 mins wait on a weekday and lunch we havent had to wait. It is a small restaurant so there's a possibility of having to wait for a table. The last time I went for lunch they had left a SUGARFISH BIRTHDAY REWARDS PROGRAM card. My birthday was coming up so I sure did sign up! The way this program works is you have to leave their your contact info and if you come 2 times before your bday on your birthdate you qualify for a free "Trust ME" on your bday. Not sure if many know about it but I did tell my bf to sign up. It seems that each time you have to fill out the card and they will record it on your account. I'm excited to go back a second time so I can qualify for my free BIRTHDAY Trust me! I live right across the street so it definitely will not be hard to come on my bday :)</Review>

<user>109815267831202318650</user>< username>
Walter Macalma<//username>
<date>1402706059728</date>< Rating>
5</Rating>
<text>There are a few things that have altered my entire understanding of sushi. The movie Giro Dreams of Sushi which highlights the Edo-Style strictly adhered to at  Sushi Nozawa and less so here at Sugarfish. With Sushi Nozawa now closed and the Nozawa Bar a little out of my price range Sugarfish has become my go for Omakase Edo-style sushi until I save enough money to fly to Japan.

I have always had immense respect for the care, skill and preparation that is involved in creating sushi at it's highest levels. All too often in my hometown our sleepy surfer vibe gets in the way over saucing rolls, losing all the nuances and purity.

Small. All of Kazunori's restaurants are small. Design is traditional, clean, uncluttered.

You will not find any rolls like the Las Vegas roll, Rainbow or anything that's beyond traditional, highlighting the fish. The rice is served warm to almost melt the cool fish without cooking it. The Toro and Blue Crab are my favorites, not sure why the cucumber roll is almost as expensive as the other rolls. They are not overstuffed pine cone's when it comes to the hand rolls. Tight and the roasted seaweed ensures the full effect and flavor profile.

I wasn't a fan of the sashimi as it's small, and I found the oyster sashimi kind of mushed, I prefer either shooters or half shelled. I was digging the organic edamame.

Uni is overpriced, but the nozawa style shrimp is pretty good value. All the tuna's are excellent, but I wish they offered grades within the toro designation. Salmon is perfectly firm. On my last trip they had monkfish liver which was the freshest I've ever had and the standard by which many sushi nuts rate restaurants.

The Trust Me Menu's are very reasonable and not meant to stuff you. These are the dinner's you should be getting. The lite has shrimp while the standard has quite a few other offerings like blue crab hand roll and halibut instead of the shrimp. TheNozawa is kind of the best of both adding snapper and the daily special nigiri. They do these to go which is great. They don't substitute and warn of this up front. No extra sauces, salt or additional rice.

I like their Nozawa sake which goes well with Orion, but for the real value go with the Ryo as the Hakkaisan is pricey at $3.50 per oz. I find it hard drinking Sapporo when the rest of the meal is so high.

Service is deliberate, inviting, but not catering or accommodating which I think at this level is understandable. Sugarfish follow in the footsteps of the original restaurant that pretty much educated California about edo and omakase. Nazi or not, it's not for everyone. They will not compromise their art and for those that want to go to Giro have the next best thing here in Sugarfish.<//text><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Response>None<//Response><GmapID>0x80c2be1386e3a105:0x163808889f1de3ce< /GmapID></record></dataset><record>
